<script>
      var googletag = googletag || {};
      googletag.cmd = googletag.cmd || [];
      googletag.cmd.push(function () {
          googletag.pubads().disableInitialLoad();
      });

      pbjs.que.push(function () {
          pbjs.addAdUnits(adUnits);
          pbjs.enableAnalytics([{
                provider: 'pubwise',
                options: {
                    site: 'd2a5ef67-8fed-4d00-9918-927ea7374a10',
                    endpoint:'https://api.pubwise.io/api/v4/event/add/'
                    }
                }]
          );
          pbjs.requestBids({
              bidsBackHandler: sendAdserverRequest
          });
      });

      function sendAdserverRequest() {
          if (pbjs.adserverRequestSent) return;
          pbjs.adserverRequestSent = true;
          googletag.cmd.push(function () {
              pbjs.que.push(function () {
                  pbjs.setTargetingForGPTAsync();
                  googletag.pubads().refresh();
              });
          });
      }

      setTimeout(function () {
          sendAdserverRequest();
      }, PREBID_TIMEOUT);

</script>

                    <td>
                            <div class="player-info-box-header team-bluejays"><div class="player-info-box-name"><h1>Randal Grichuk</h1><div class="player-info-box-name-team"><a href="/teams/bluejays">Toronto Blue Jays</a></div></div><div class="player-info-box-item">Age: 26</div><div class="player-info-box-item">Bats/Throws: R/R</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-item">6' 1" / 205</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-pos">OF</div></div>
                        <div class="player-info-bio">
                            <strong>Birthdate: </strong>8/13/1991 (26 y, 7 m, 16 d)<br /><b>Drafted:</b> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=10243&position=OF#draft" style="text-decoration:none;">2009 June Amateur Draft - Round: 1, Pick: 24, Overall: 24, Team: Los Angeles Angels</a><br /><strong>Contract:</strong> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=10243&position=OF#contract" >$2.6M / 1 Years (2018)</a>
                        </div>
                    </td>

                    
                    <tr><td><hr class="player-page-info-sep"/><div class="player-page-rotowire"><strong><a href="https://www.rotowire.com/users/ad_jump.asp?id=688&playerid=10998">RotoWire News</a>:</strong> Grichuk (ribs) is in Saturday's lineup batting fourth and playing right field, Shi Davidi of Sportsnet.ca reports. (3/24/2018)</div></td></tr>

                </tr>
                <tr><td><hr class="player-page-info-sep"/><table class="player-page-news"><tr>
                    <td>1/22/2018</td><td class="td-badge"><div class="fg badge">FG</div></td><td><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/the-depreciating-randal-grichuk/">The Depreciating Randal Grichuk</a><span class="m_author"> by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/index.php?author=7030">Jeff Sullivan</a></span></td></tr><tr>
                    <td>1/19/2018</td><td class="td-badge"><div class="fg badge">FG</div></td><td><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/randal-grichuk-is-above-average-for-the-blue-jays/">Randal Grichuk Is Above Average for the Blue Jays</a><span class="m_author"> by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/index.php?author=16">Carson Cistulli</a></span></td></tr><tr>

                    <td>4/16/2017</td><td class="td-badge"><div class="rg badge">RG</div></td><td><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/the-sleeper-and-the-bust-episode-446-making-a-judgment-call/">The Sleeper and the Bust Episode: 446  Making a J&#8230;</a><span class="m_author"> by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/index.php?author=11752">Paul Sporer</a></span></td></tr></table></div></td></tr>
            
            </table>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
        
        
        
        
        
        
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Grichuk got his first taste of the majors in 2014, and will likely break camp as a member of the 25-man roster to start 2015. The problem with the 24-year-old is that he will mostly start against lefties, due to his severe platoon issues. He has a .954 minor-league OPS against lefties, but just .736 against right-handers. He could have some value as a plug-and-play streaming option when the Cards face lefties, but he's not someone you're going to want on your roster for more than a couple days at a time. (Scott Strandberg)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>You can never get too excited about the fantasy potential of a guy on the wrong side of a platoon.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>At some point last season, people started to notice Grichuk's loud contact. Over 466 career plate appearances, he's posted Stantonian hard hit rates. His 302 foot average fly ball distance ranked 23rd in baseball last season. An injury also negatively affected his hard hit numbers. He was doing even better before landing on the disabled list. Clearly, he makes seriously authoritative contact. Before the hype train runs out of control, there are red flags to address. He has serious contact issues coupled with questionable plate discipline (31.4% strikeouts, 6.3% walks). His .365 batting average on balls in play looks fluky, especially in light of a 10% infield fly ball rate. When almost 40% of your plate appearances end in an automatic out, it's hard to maintain a better than .220 average. Rather than the next Giancarlo Stanton, I see a more athletic Evan Gattis -- one who can play a passable center field. He's just 24 years old, so he still has time to improve too. Overall, he's one of the most exciting and volatile young players in the league. (Brad Johnson)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Grichuk comes with serious power, iffy plate discipline, and contact issues. That he can play center field ensures an every day role with above average production. There's a massive ceiling lurking under the surface, but it's more reasonable to expect merely above average production.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Randal Grichuk can hit the ball really hard with his swing all but yelling I AM RANDAL. Offensively, that might be his only skill, but it has been good enough to get regular playing time the last two years and an expected starting role in 2017 for the Cardinals. Grichuk doesn't walk very much, just six percent last season, and he strikes out a bit too often, 30% of his plate appearances. At the beginning of last season, Grichuk tried a more patient approach, walking a little more, striking out a bit less. It worked, except he lost his power. He switched things up and had a strong second half. When he squares the ball up good things tend to happen. Last season, Grichuk had more extra-base hits than singles with 24 homers, three triples, and 29 doubles compared to just 51 singles. Grichuk has good speed, but hasn't been able to turn that into anything in terms of base stealing, as he had just five steals while getting caught four times last season. His strikeouts are going to limit his average so when he steps up to the plate, just hope for the long ball. If he gets a full season of playing time, he might hit 30 homers. (Craig Edwards)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Randal Grichuk can hit homers, but not much else. He should have a full season of playing time to get close to 30 homers, but don't get your hopes up for any other categories.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>
